  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8475f1ff-d4c2-4474-ae6d-b177278ef968'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText7717116003761540691" style="display:none">الرواية الجديدة للكاتب والصحفي إبراهيم عيسى، والتي يتناول من خلالها ظاهرة بعض شيوخ الفضائيات التي انتشرت في العالم العربي في السنوات الأخيرة، حيث يكشف لنا العالم الخفي لهؤلاء الشيوخ، والعلاقات التي تربطهم بأجهزة الأمن والساسة ورجال الأعمال، وهي رواية جريئة توضح كيف يساء استخدام الدين.<br /><br />يقول إبراهيم عيسى عن روايته الجديدة: "بدأت كتابة هذه الرواية عام 2009 وأنا أعارض الرئيس السابق، وأثناء محاكماتي ثم فصلي من الدستور، ثم منعي من الكتابة حتى قامت الثورة، ومرورنا بالمرحلة الانتقالية، واستمررت في الكتابة حتى مارس الماضي 2012، إنها من أعز الروايات إلى قلبي".<br /><br />من أجواء الرواية:<br /><br />"أدرك أنور أن هذه لحظة ذروة، خصوصاً مع إلحاح المخرج من غرفة التحكم في همس يملأ السماعة المدسوسة في طبلة أذنه يطالبه:<br />- فاصل يا أنور، الإعلانات تنزل هنا.<br /> والكل سخن يريد سماع الإجابة.<br />حين خرج أنور بالحلقة إلى فاصل صاح الشيخ حاتم:<br />- يا ولاد العفريتة تعملوها في الناس، فيه دلوقتِ ثلاثة أربعة مليون بيتفرجوا حيموتوا عايزين يعرفوا إيه حكاية زوجة جاره دي.<br />سمع صوت المخرج صارخًا بالفخر:<br />- شفت «الساسبنس» يا مولانا؟"</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31433660-the-televangelist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16127160-chavelli-sulikowska?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16127160-chavelli-sulikowska?shelf=five-star">five-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16127160-chavelli-sulikowska?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3112864094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12148454489154952424">So i'm living in Egypt and never having read an Egyptian author, I was spoilt for choice of contemporary Arabic authors at the American University Bookstore in Cairo! I could have started with Naguib Mahfouz, but decided on something more modern...I have plenty of time to get to the literary giant that is Mahfouz in the Arabic literary canon. <br/><br/>I have to admit, it was the title and modernist cover of the Televangelist that attracted me first, then the blurb on the back had me sold - it sounded bot</span>
  <span id="freeText12148454489154952424" style="display:none">So i'm living in Egypt and never having read an Egyptian author, I was spoilt for choice of contemporary Arabic authors at the American University Bookstore in Cairo! I could have started with Naguib Mahfouz, but decided on something more modern...I have plenty of time to get to the literary giant that is Mahfouz in the Arabic literary canon. <br /><br />I have to admit, it was the title and modernist cover of the Televangelist that attracted me first, then the blurb on the back had me sold - it sounded both controversial and comedic, and it certainly doesn't fall short on either of these qualities, in fact it has both in abundance. <br /><br />The protagonist, Sheik Hatem el-Shenawi, is a bit like an Islamic version of Dr Phil. The host and star of a popular talk show with live audience and Q and A on all matters Quranic, he is both charismatic and confident, suave and a bit too self assured in his own knowledge. He has the gift of the gab and at times even astounds himself with his effortless ability to digest the complexities of the Quran and make Islam comprehensible to the masses...until....the Sheik gets drawn against his will into an intricate plot loaded with political intrigue, corruption and scandal that threatens to bring his seemingly idyllic world crumbling down around him. <br /><br />Setting off a series of catastrophic about turns, the Sheik is forced to confront and atone not only the haunting ghosts of his past but also question the very foundation of his belief. Monumental self upheaval begins amidst a climatic build to catastrophe as we follow the Sheik's journey of true but fearful self reflection as he navigates the direction of his moral compass.<br /><br />An immensely enjoyable political satire, a modern comedy of errors, with literally laugh out loud moments and exceptionally witty dialogue. Nonetheless, Essa's novel serves as a more serious examination of the collective power of religion in the modern world and the critical importance of always questioning what we decide to place our faith in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12148454489154952424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2902397587?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kumasama" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kumasama" href="/user/show/100050881-kumasama">Kumasama</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6235684615527487790">*Score: 8.5/10*<br/><br/>Summary: A character study about a highly acclaimed and well respected Sheik in Egypt. Through his prespective, a lot of political and religious topics are discussed as well as his own life struggles. <br/><br/>Pros:<br/><br/>- Immensely satisfying character study handling multiple character layers expertly<br/>- The main character is relatable in many ways, and is very easy to like and connect to his struggles<br/>- Many interconnected small stories within a larger whole that integrate very well<br/>- Author handl</span>
  <span id="freeText6235684615527487790" style="display:none">*Score: 8.5/10*<br /><br />Summary: A character study about a highly acclaimed and well respected Sheik in Egypt. Through his prespective, a lot of political and religious topics are discussed as well as his own life struggles. <br /><br />Pros:<br /><br />- Immensely satisfying character study handling multiple character layers expertly<br />- The main character is relatable in many ways, and is very easy to like and connect to his struggles<br />- Many interconnected small stories within a larger whole that integrate very well<br />- Author handles many sensetive topics very professionally, never sounding like he is preaching while stating clearly his views on such matters through the characters - he is always bold but also fair and ensures multiple prespectives are presented<br />- Author's expression of a father's love of his son is spot on<br />- So many themes and ideas, gives the mind a lot to think about<br /><br />Cons:<br /><br />- A couple of the twists were very predictable, and a bit cliche<br />- One of the female characters had potential to show more depth, but instead was used as a plot device<br />- Its a large book, and while it mostly flows and has strong pacing, there are very brief but notable points that pacing slows considerabely<br /><br />Overall: If you don't mind dealing with some very sensetive religious themes, and open to hear multiple views and interpretations, this books provides a lot to think about. There is no sense of judgement and preaching, hence the book never assaults your own beliefs and instead provides a wide pool of thoughts and ideas, all researched very well. In addition, if you are a fan of the "character study" gnere, this offers a stellar main character that you can't help but feel for his struggles and plights. Its an enriching reading experience that is highly recommended, and is easily the best arabic book i have read so far.</span>

<div id="review_2268353661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268353661" />
    <a title="Mark Farag" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12772399-mark-farag"><img alt="Mark Farag" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572778725p2/12772399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268353661?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Farag" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Farag" href="/user/show/12772399-mark-farag">Mark Farag</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29913717-the-televangelist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268353661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8624206296434116874">At first this book seemed particularly cowardly as it presented the issue of a Muslim converting to Christianity (a massive taboo in any Muslim country) and then seemingly dismissed it as a psychiatric issue. But as always with Egyptian intellectuals, their fiction is simply a thinly veiled attempt to write non fiction that is too controversial for them to defend.<br/><br/>While I disagrees profoundly with many of the opinions of Sheikh Hatem in the book (who is used by Ibrahim Eissa as a mouthpiece for h</span>
  <span id="freeText8624206296434116874" style="display:none">At first this book seemed particularly cowardly as it presented the issue of a Muslim converting to Christianity (a massive taboo in any Muslim country) and then seemingly dismissed it as a psychiatric issue. But as always with Egyptian intellectuals, their fiction is simply a thinly veiled attempt to write non fiction that is too controversial for them to defend.<br /><br />While I disagrees profoundly with many of the opinions of Sheikh Hatem in the book (who is used by Ibrahim Eissa as a mouthpiece for his more controversial opinions, a deconstruction of the 'television sheikh' in egypt and the stifling force of the government). I realise that the fact he even wrote this book is extremely brave, and its social, religious and political commentary covers things which are extremely taboo in Egypt and the Muslim world (for context many authors such as Farag Foda have been killed for similar bravery).<br /><br />The book also taught me a lot more about Islam, or rather some of the positions that are taken by more Liberal Muslim thinkers with regard to interpretation of the Quran and Hadith (which I'm admittedly ignorant on). As a result I benefitted intellectually from this book, as will most people, even if they don't agree with the opinions it presents.<br /><br />The plot while at times predictable and at others slow, was also commendable, particularly the last quarter of the book, in which Sheikh Hatem finally becomes a lovable and sympathetic character. While I had issues with the portrayal of copts in the book I realise that Ibrahim Eissa was already too brazen in his critical discussion of the Islamic clerics and government; any perceived flattery of the copts would be a further slight top far.<br /><br />In conclusion, this book was by no means a comfortable read, while a page turner, it elicited strong emotions that were not always positive in me while I read it. However, upon finishing it and reflecting, I have realised that it has given me perspective and knowledge of opinions which mirror that of people I would otherwise never meet in real life. Well done Ibrahim Eissa</span>
  <a data-text-id="8624206296434116874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2925704201?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BeesReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BeesReads" href="/user/show/75986843-beesreads">BeesReads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789774167188" href="/book/show/26366877-the-televangelist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75986843-beesreads?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2925704201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4467240533707037102">A relatively contemporary book. Some of the incidents he describes - dodgy fatwa about breast feeding, church bombing - took place while I lived in Cairo. I think the experience of living there for several years certainly helps to understand some of the goings-on with the security, tv and so on. In fact, I lived just 2km down the road from Media Production City, location for the tv programme.<br/><br/>The author is an Egyptian journalist and tv personality and has had his own run-ins with state security.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText4467240533707037102" style="display:none">A relatively contemporary book. Some of the incidents he describes - dodgy fatwa about breast feeding, church bombing - took place while I lived in Cairo. I think the experience of living there for several years certainly helps to understand some of the goings-on with the security, tv and so on. In fact, I lived just 2km down the road from Media Production City, location for the tv programme.<br /><br />The author is an Egyptian journalist and tv personality and has had his own run-ins with state security.<br /><br />There's a big secret and Hatem (the preacher) is asked to resolve the situation. Can't say more without giving away a key element of the book though the reader finds out very early on. How Hatem and the other party proceed is about 2/3 of the book.<br /><br />There are some discussions on aspects of Islamic theology and muslim history which I found interesting.<br /><br />There is a point where an attempt is made to destroy the reputation of another preacher by making accusations that he is a shia and in league with Iran. (Egypt is a predominantly sunni muslim country.)<br /><br />The book ends with a dreadful deed and also suggests a further book may be forthcoming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4467240533707037102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17657635729483630504">What an excellent book! It is super funny, the writing is very smart and engaging. The topic is timely, and the criticism of society's ignorance when it comes to understanding it's own religion is dead on. <br/><br/>I wan't that excited about the series of events unfolding at the end as I didn't really feel like the book needed to go that extra mile and present the "punch line." the book is fantastic in its simplicity and humor, and content, and didn't need any inserted action in my opinion. <br/>Nonetheless, </span>
  <span id="freeText17657635729483630504" style="display:none">What an excellent book! It is super funny, the writing is very smart and engaging. The topic is timely, and the criticism of society's ignorance when it comes to understanding it's own religion is dead on. <br /><br />I wan't that excited about the series of events unfolding at the end as I didn't really feel like the book needed to go that extra mile and present the "punch line." the book is fantastic in its simplicity and humor, and content, and didn't need any inserted action in my opinion. <br />Nonetheless, it didn't take away from the overall message of the story.<br /><br /> I am just saddened that this book was not the "Booker Award" winner. A much better book than ساق البامبو with all respect to the author. <br /><br /> *note: apologies for writing the review in English. </span>

  <span id="freeText5586722842644902788" style="display:none">Okay this is actually my first review in goodreads so i din't really know how to do this. Anyway, I actually bought this book last year (2017) and read it on late January 2018 which mainly because i am out of books. The first time I read this was just after I bought it and i put it back to the shelf because the first hundred is to me quite a lot. too much to process and maybe there are few unnecessary subplot that to me is unfinished.<br /><br />But, what I like about this book is that the main character, The Mawlana; Hatem El Shenawy is very clear since the whole story is through his narrative and i find that the character development is very good. <br /><br />the whole books to me, is interesting to read but I don't necessarily like it as I don't really get some part of (or maybe it's just me). it's packed with information which i'm not sure true or not but I would like to applaud the writer for the ability to expand the story to the end while making it make sense at last which i wish i can write more of this review but i am to lazy, pardon me.<br /><br />okay, let's write a little more, shall me. I am not satisfied with two particular character, Omayma and Boutros or Hassan which i find both are not well polished as they both are kind of the important figures in story line. <span id="freeTextContainer7306993191233065840">Mixed impression. On the one hand I enjoyed a refreshing plot. I had never read anything like it before. I can say I had some historic and cultural insight. Egyptian cultural and religious dualism. Copts versus muslims. People vs totalitarian government. Religion and business. It was a bit disappointing and it left a bad aftert</span>
  <span id="freeText7306993191233065840" style="display:none">Mixed impression. On the one hand I enjoyed a refreshing plot. I had never read anything like it before. I can say I had some historic and cultural insight. Egyptian cultural and religious dualism. Copts versus muslims. People vs totalitarian government. Religion and business. It's well paced and engaging, even funny at times. <br /><br />On the other hand the protagonist turned out to be weaker than I wanted him to be given that he was a man of knowledge. It was a bit disappointing and it left a bad aftertaste. -1 star for that. <br /><br />Also, I couldn't quiet work out where the author stands in all this. Apparently he tried to bring up some timely controversial issues of his culture one of them being the fact that people know next to nothing about their religion and only pay lip service to tolerance and many others.<br /><br />I will not spoil it for you though by giving any further details.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fCo++UdPpRYLebk04ZTpz6qvqY+Oh29/fS7WgwdyCWHrk6S/A8KmPLMFWGJxcG/ZIbbhtVn2HpR8Dhkmf4sdeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jjFPJG2F3koSdnIwxZSjbmGLmsXPjG60Ayz8nc1VscMZiNViKQjdYKoKk2ZVcCV46pLS/xj9H18CDDM4tayl2A==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1340291._">About إبراهيم عيسى</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1340291._"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1271692543p3/1340291.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/1340291._">إبراهيم عيسى

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5035261830632502402">إبراهيم عيسى، صحفي مصري. وتولى رئاسة تحرير صحيفة الدستور المصرية اليومية حتّىٰ أقاله مالك الجريدة السيد البدوي في أكتوبر 2010 بسبب إصراره على نشر مقالة لمحمد البرادعي عن حرب أكتوبر.<br/><br/>التحق بالعمل في مجلة روز اليوسف منذ أن كان طالباً في السنة الأولى من كلية الإعلام. يتولى الآن رئاسة تحرير صحيفة الدستور اليومية واسعة الانتشار في مصر، كما أنه أحد أعضاء الهيئة الاستشارية للشبكة العربية لمعلومات حقوق الإ</span>
  <span id="freeText5035261830632502402" style="display:none">إبراهيم عيسى، صحفي مصري. وتولى رئاسة تحرير صحيفة الدستور المصرية اليومية حتّىٰ أقاله مالك الجريدة السيد البدوي في أكتوبر 2010 بسبب إصراره على نشر مقالة لمحمد البرادعي عن حرب أكتوبر.<br /><br />التحق بالعمل في مجلة روز اليوسف منذ أن كان طالباً في السنة الأولى من كلية الإعلام. يتولى الآن رئاسة تحرير صحيفة الدستور اليومية واسعة الانتشار في مصر، كما أنه أحد أعضاء الهيئة الاستشارية للشبكة العربية لمعلومات حقوق الإنسان. يقدم برنامج الفهرس إسبوعياً على قناة دريم الفضائية، كما كان يقدم برنامج سياسي اسمه على القهوة في نفس القناة إلى أن منعت السلطات المصرية بثه. وتتميز كتاباته باسلوب ساخر وتلقائي ثاقب وعميق في الوصف والتشبيه كما إنه سهل ممتنع يتسلل إلى قلب القارىء بمهارة وحنكة بالغة.يمكن اعتباره أكثر الصحفيين المصريين نشاطاً وإحتجاجاً على ممارسات السلطة السياسية في مصر، ونتيجة لمواقفه أغلقت له ثلاث صحف كان يرأس تحريرها كما صودرت إحدى رواياته (مقتل الرجل الكبير) وله أيضا رواية أشباح مصرية.<br /><br />تم إتهامه بالسب والقذف والتحريض والإهانة والتطاول على رئيس الجمهورية هو والصحفية سحر زكي والمحامي سعيد عبد الله وذلك عندما كتبت الصحفية سحر مقالاً بجريدة الدستور تحت عنوان مواطن من وراق العرب يطالب بمحاكمة مبارك وأسرته ورد مبلغ 500 مليار جنيه قيمة القطاع العام والمعونات الخارجية. في 26 يونيو 2006 حكم عليه بالسجن لمدة عام وكفالة 10 ألاف جنيه، غير أن محكمة الاستئناف خففت الحكم إلى غرامة تصل إلى 4000 دولار.<br /><br />تعرض لمحاكمات من قبل أجهزة الأمن المصرية بتهمة نشر أخبار كاذبة عن صحة رئيس الجمهورية، وصدر يوم 13 سبتمبر 2007 حكم ضده بالسجن سنة، وتمت إعادة محاكمته أمام دائرة أخرى و التي أصدرت في 28 سبتمبر 2008 حكمها عليه بالحبس لمدة شهرين، وكان الحكم مشمول بوجوبية النفاذ فسلم نفسه للسلطات في نفس اليوم، ولكن الرئيس حسني مبارك أصدر قراراً جمهورياً بالعفو عنه في 6 أكتوبر 2008.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5035261830632502402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/21397436">Quotes from مولانا</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;إذا كان المسلمون يعتقدون أن إسلام شخص مسيحي منفعة للإسلام فهذا اعتقاد واهم، وسببه شعور المسلمين بأنهم أقل قدرة وإمكانات وقوة في العالم، فهو نوع من التعويض، وفي مصر بالذات هو نوع من الشعور بالانتصار في واقع كله هزائم كأن لو أسلم مسيحي يبقى المسلمون بقوا أفضل وأحسن وكأنهم كسبوا معركة وأثبتوا أن الإسلام أفضل من المسيحية. هذه طبعًا مشاعر المسلمين محدودي الدخل ومحدودي العقل ومحدودي الانتصارات في الحياة. ثم وسط حالة فساد يرتع فيها الكل فهذه وسيلة للتطهر والتقرب من الله من وجهة نظرهم.<br />أما المسيحيون فيرون في تنصُّر مسلم معجزة نورانية تنتقم لهم من غطرسة وغرور المسلمين الذين يتعاملون كأنهم الأفضل والأعظم، وانتصارًا للأقلية في مواجهة الأغلبية التي تعذب النصارى بالتجاهل سواء بصوت الميكروفونات بالأذان والصلاة في أذن المسيحي وخطب الجمعة ودروس التليفزيون التي تُكفّر النصارى كل يوم، فلما ينجح المسيحيون في تنصير مسلم يبقى عيدًا وإعلانًا للنصر. وهذا كله لا تراه في أوروبا مثلًا [...] لماذا؟ لأنه مجتمع غير مهزوم، ولا يتخذ الدين والعقيدة بابًا للتعويض عن وضع اقتصادي مهبب أو حرية مخنوقة أو فراغ سياسي أو قلة قيمة وانعدام حيلة.&rdquo;</span>
